<div id="review_3510452802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3510452802" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3510452802?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/51031906-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=japanese-literature">japanese-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=world-literature">world-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=art">art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=tokyo">tokyo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=women-in-translation">women-in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=women-s-literature">women-s-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=japan">japan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3510452802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13881138593277307329"><b>
  <i>‘’It is the start of another day, the time when the world wakes up and the cogs of society begin to move. I am one of those cogs, going round and round. I have become a functioning part of the world, rotating in the time of day called morning.’’</i>
</b><br/><br/>Keiko has been working in the same convenience store in Tokyo for eighteen years. She is not interested in finding a new job, she doesn’t particularly want to hang out with her few acquaintances, and having a family of her own or even a relationship h</span>
  <span id="freeText13881138593277307329" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘’It is the start of another day, the time when the world wakes up and the cogs of society begin to move. I am one of those cogs, going round and round. I have become a functioning part of the world, rotating in the time of day called morning.’’</i>
</b><br /><br />Keiko has been working in the same convenience store in Tokyo for eighteen years. She is not interested in finding a new job, she doesn’t particularly want to hang out with her few acquaintances, and having a family of her own or even a relationship has never crossed her mind. And even though her family loves her, they are afraid she’s not going to ‘’make it’’ in the ‘’real world’’. Whatever that means, anyway. Keiko needs instructions so as not to be ‘’different’’. Working in the Hiromachi Station Smile Mart allows her to function under an umbrella of specific patterns of behaviour. When a (disgusting to the core) young man comes to work in the store, he unwittingly provides Keiko with the chance to understand that the problem lies with the others, not herself.<br /><br /> <b>
  <i>‘’From now on, we existed only in the service of the convenience store.’’</i>
</b><br /><br />Sayaka Murata creates a superb story, set in a vivid urban setting, in the heart of Tokyo. Within the boundaries of the store, we understand that rules dictating what to wear, how to speak, how to smile need to be obeyed. So there is no room for individuality, and there are limited opportunities to advance. And that’s fine. Let’s face it, most jobs are the same. We can’t just walk right into our classrooms, our private practices, our shops, our offices and start dancing naked, screaming profanities. We all wear our ‘’work’’ uniform every day, we all obey to job rules, strict or less strict, and this is completely understandable. For me, and for Keiko, the dangerous territory is the world outside, the terrain of obligatory socializing and social rules that have no basis anymore, yet need to be fulfilled. Why? Don’t ask me, I don’t know. Ask those who enjoy mingling and getting married…<br /><br /> <b>
  <i>‘’When something was strange, everyone thought they had the right to come stomping in all over your life to figure out why. I found that arrogant and infuriating, not to mention a pain in the neck. Sometimes I even wanted to hit them with a shovel to shut them up, like I did that time in elementary school.’’</i>
</b><br /><br />Keiko is my spirit animal. Enough said.<br /><br />She is tremendously perceptive. Her observations on people’s behaviour and facial expressions are spot on. The insults are constant, coming from ‘’friends’’, but Keiko doesn’t respond. She doesn’t know how. Until she finally lifts her head and strikes back, exhausted by the abominable behaviour of a man who embodies all that is fake, cheap and toxic in the construction of a society where women and men believe they have the right to meddle with one’s life just because she doesn’t want to ‘’find someone’’. This is a society that will cast you out if you’re not interested in sex or money. This is a society with an orgasmic fixation on age, motherhood, social status and wealth. This is superficiality in its most extreme, tormenting, tyrannical form. And Keiko sends each one of them to Hell because she can.<br /><br />Clever and funny, and quite unsettling, even shocking at times, this gem of Japanese Literature is a quirky, yet poignant story of individualism, choice, expectations and a monstrous society. Absolutely wonderful!<br /><br /> <b>
  <i>‘’No. It’s not a matter of whether they permit it or not. It’s what I am.’’</i>
</b><br /><br />My reviews can also be found on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theopinionatedreaderblog.wordpress.com/">https://theopinionatedreaderblog.word...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13881138593277307329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2879035055" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2879035055" />
    <a title="Brandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice"><img alt="Brandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582594594p2/36348070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2879035055?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandice" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice">Brandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/38357895-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2879035055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5046379627639089608"><i>Convenience Store Woman</i> as described by author Jami Attenberg: <i>”What a weird and wonderful and deeply satisfying book this is.”</i> <br/><br/>For the most part, I felt the same way about it. This is a slim book, with a simple premise: 36-year old Keiko Furukura is a convenience store worker and has been for the last 18 years. She doesn’t have a serious relationship (nor has she ever had one) and she has only a few friends. It appears her life has not progressed over the last several years. She is whole-hearte</span>
  <span id="freeText5046379627639089608" style="display:none"><i>Convenience Store Woman</i> as described by author Jami Attenberg: <i>”What a weird and wonderful and deeply satisfying book this is.”</i> <br /><br />For the most part, I felt the same way about it. This is a slim book, with a simple premise: 36-year old Keiko Furukura is a convenience store worker and has been for the last 18 years. She doesn’t have a serious relationship (nor has she ever had one) and she has only a few friends. It appears her life has not progressed over the last several years. She is whole-heartedly committed to her life as a store worker and has no aspirations to achieve more, in any sense. The book is about Keiko’s day-to-day life and how it’s impacted by a new male coworker she encounters at the store. <br /><br /><i>Convenience Store Woman</i> is equal parts amusing and sad. I felt bad for Keiko and her general social obliviousness, but also found some of her actions and commentary entertaining. This book is a reminder that we don’t all always want the same things and success is subjective. It was a quick, worthwhile little read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5046379627639089608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2486757439" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2486757439" />
    <a title="Greta G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45248887-greta-g"><img alt="Greta G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525435609p2/45248887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2486757439?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greta G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greta G" href="/user/show/45248887-greta-g">Greta G</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40778245-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45248887-greta-g?shelf=japan">japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45248887-greta-g?shelf=owned-in-english">owned-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45248887-greta-g?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45248887-greta-g?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2486757439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1963393014732150197">Keiko Furukura is a 36-year old woman who works part-time in a convenience store and lives in an old, tiny apartment. She has never fallen in love and isn’t interested in a sexual relationship. <br/>Although she’s perfectly content with her life and with the daily routine of her job as a store worker, people in her little social circle find her odd and put pressure on her to become more ‘acceptable’ by finding a decent job and by getting married. <br/>Keiko realizes she’s considered a ‘foreign object’, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText1963393014732150197" style="display:none">Keiko Furukura is a 36-year old woman who works part-time in a convenience store and lives in an old, tiny apartment. She has never fallen in love and isn’t interested in a sexual relationship. <br />Although she’s perfectly content with her life and with the daily routine of her job as a store worker, people in her little social circle find her odd and put pressure on her to become more ‘acceptable’ by finding a decent job and by getting married. <br />Keiko realizes she’s considered a ‘foreign object’, but she doesn’t know how to be more ‘ordinary’ outside of the convenience store ; unlike a convenience store, life has no written manual. <br /><i>”The convenience store worker mask is the only one I’m fit to wear. So if people don’t accept that, I have no idea what I can do about it.”</i><br />To be honest, I didn’t care much about this story. Most of it takes place in the convenience store, and the daily routine of a store isn’t all that interesting. The dialogues were repetitive and it also felt to me that the author tried a little too hard to put her message across, namely non-conformity, diversity is okay. <br /><br />However Keiko isn’t just a nonconformist, odd or eccentric person. She seemed mentally impaired - possibly autistic - which made the message rather confusing to me. The way I see it, people usually have <i>lower expectations</i> of a mentally impaired person, and would be more than happy if that person has a satisfactory job and is able to live independently, so the message didn’t ring true to me and I agree with Sam Quixote’s statement in his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2480869947?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">excellent review</a> on the book :<br /><i>“I feel like there’s a good novel somewhere in ‘Convenience Store Woman’ but Syaka Murata didn’t realise it. Her commentary on conformist society and the individual is inane and unoriginal though far worse is her muddled placement of the main character within that commentary.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1963393014732150197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2645681174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2645681174" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73431206-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525868884p2/73431206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2645681174?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/73431206-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40778245-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73431206-richard?shelf=current-lit-wd">current-lit-wd</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2645681174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17927673976703317249">‘The normal world has no room for exceptions and always quietly eliminates foreign objects. Anyone who is lacking is disposed of.’<br/><br/>Deep in the gleaming new business district of Hiiromachi, a Tokyo suburb, is a convenience store. In this clean, controlled and brightly lit world we meet Keiko Furukura.<br/>She has worked here, part time, for 18 years and her life is defined by her work. <br/>Keiko lives for the routine of the store and the comfort of familiarity. She relishes the idea of being a ‘useable too</span>
  <span id="freeText17927673976703317249" style="display:none">‘The normal world has no room for exceptions and always quietly eliminates foreign objects. Anyone who is lacking is disposed of.’<br /><br />Deep in the gleaming new business district of Hiiromachi, a Tokyo suburb, is a convenience store. In this clean, controlled and brightly lit world we meet Keiko Furukura.<br />She has worked here, part time, for 18 years and her life is defined by her work. <br />Keiko lives for the routine of the store and the comfort of familiarity. She relishes the idea of being a ‘useable tool’ and worries that if she were to leave her job she would be ‘........ downgraded from store worker to female of the human species’. <br />Keiko doesn’t feel comfortable discussing or even thinking about her private life and can’t comprehend how it is that her co workers are more interested in her love life than sorting out the lunchtime special promotion of rice balls and cheese frankfurters! It’s all very mystifying to her.<br />The self Keiko Furukura presents to the world is defined by her coworkers. She doesn’t connect in an ordinary way with the world around her, she doesn’t get the nuances of human interaction, she can’t empathise, and ........... she knows it. She studies the random variety of people she works with and copies how they speak, what they wear and how they interact with each other.<br />We have begun to suspect that Keiko Furukura is somewhere firmly on the autistic spectrum.<br />The novel examines how society demands we should behave, what is considered ‘normal’ and how someone who is somewhat ‘different’ can find a way of being accepted.<br />When Keiko’s ordered existence collides with Shiraha an angry, misogynistic, self confessed loser, she has to re-evaluate the meaning of her life.<br />The writing in Convenience Store Woman is simple, precise and slightly detached, a style I’ve encountered and enjoyed before in other Japanese novels.<br />I really liked this slim novel ......... a wryly humorous and thoughtful read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17927673976703317249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11350907594255829076"><br/><br/> 3.5 <br/> 
  <em>
    <strong>An odd little book with quite eccentric characters</strong>
  </em>
 <br/>Keiko is the quirky protagonist and she decides that working in a convenience store is both satisfying and provides her with a sense of belonging. She feels very "connected" to the store and its routines and mundane tasks.  She doesn't mind this, she thrives and enjoys her job and is a hard worker.<br/><br/>Her family constantly worries that she is "not normal."  Society has certain "expectations" and she has chosen not to comply.  There</span>
  <span id="freeText11350907594255829076" style="display:none"><br /><br /> 3.5 <br /> 
  <em>
    <strong>An odd little book with quite eccentric characters</strong>
  </em>
 <br />Keiko is the quirky protagonist and she decides that working in a convenience store is both satisfying and provides her with a sense of belonging. She feels very "connected" to the store and its routines and mundane tasks.  She doesn't mind this, she thrives and enjoys her job and is a hard worker.<br /><br />Her family constantly worries that she is "not normal."  Society has certain "expectations" and she has chosen not to comply.  There is a deeper message about life and the assumptions that all successful people are expected to follow, but Keiko isn't listening!<br /><br />This is a quiet story about acceptance and judgement. I enjoyed spending time with Keiko!<br /><br />Publication date is June 22,2018. Thanks to NG/Grove Press for the ARC.<br /><br /> <br /><br /> </span>

<div id="review_3540256707" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3540256707" />
    <a title="Robin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36555254-robin"><img alt="Robin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536187488p2/36555254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3540256707?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin" href="/user/show/36555254-robin">Robin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/38357895-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=japan">japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=translation">translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3540256707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10008245257952939783"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600388157i/30120967._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A look at the game of life. Remember that board game? Ever play it back in the day? Spin the wheel, go to university, get a job, get married, have kids, and cash in at the end. Everyone who plays lives happily ever after.<br/><br/>The rules are pretty simple, but for Miss Furukura, it's a baffling game. She's never understood how to play, how to act. Figuring out what is "normal" never came naturally. She even mimics the cadence of those around her in order to sound human when she talks. At the age of eig</span>
  <span id="freeText10008245257952939783" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600388157i/30120967._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A look at the game of life. Remember that board game? Ever play it back in the day? Spin the wheel, go to university, get a job, get married, have kids, and cash in at the end. Everyone who plays lives happily ever after.<br><br>The rules are pretty simple, but for Miss Furukura, it's a baffling game. She's never understood how to play, how to act. Figuring out what is "normal" never came naturally. She even mimics the cadence of those around her in order to sound human when she talks. At the age of eighteen, she gets a job in a convenience store, the only place she feels at home. Eighteen years later, she is still there, still shouting out greetings, still ringing in purchases, still tending to displays with deep devotion.<br><br>At first, working in the convenience store was a good move in the game of her life. But all this time later, she looks more and more conspicuous. A weirdo. A weirdo without a "real" job, without a husband or even boyfriend. No little pink or blue pegs in her car - forget those - she's a virgin. She's a shame to her family. She causes people around her to feel uncomfortable. What to make of this person?<br><br>One day, she meets an equally weird character, a guy who can't hack it as a convenience store worker. They come to a mutually beneficial arrangement, but can two weirdos really fool the world into thinking they can play the game? More importantly, can they fool themselves?<br><br>This very short novella (or long short story - not sure what to call it) provides much food for thought on the idea of life as a machine, and how we rely on other people to play certain roles for our own comfort. If they don't play along, will the machine keep working? If they don't play along, then why the hell am I?<br><br>As I said, it's very interesting, though I think I'd have liked it to go further than it did. Something about this story felt safe to me - maybe because I know how far off the page this author can go (please, if you're brave, read Murata's novel <i>Earthlings</i> - it's a wild ride!). This story stayed ensconced in the firm grip of the convenience store. And how exciting can that possibly get?</span>
  <a data-text-id="10008245257952939783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=translated_into_german">translated_into_german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=japanese-lit">japanese-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2360782264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2691050715494347408"><em>Published in English as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38357895.Convenience_Store_Woman' title='Convenience Store Woman by Sayaka Murata' rel='nofollow noopener'>Convenience Store Woman</a></em><br/><br/>Anyone who's ever gone shopping for groceries must have a thing or two to rant about employees. You're late, but still need to nip in to buy that little something before getting to work, yet the shop assistant is taking his/her sweet time chatting about that totally hilarious (you had to be there!) story. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523994020ra/25392809.gif' alt='chop chop' width='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Not Keiko Furukura! After 18 years, she's so well attuned to the sounds of the convenience store, that she can react even to the slightest change </span>
  <span id="freeText2691050715494347408" style="display:none"><em>Published in English as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38357895.Convenience_Store_Woman" title="Convenience Store Woman by Sayaka Murata" rel="nofollow noopener">Convenience Store Woman</a></em><br><br>Anyone who's ever gone shopping for groceries must have a thing or two to rant about employees. You're late, but still need to nip in to buy that little something before getting to work, yet the shop assistant is taking his/her sweet time chatting about that totally hilarious (you had to be there!) story. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523994020ra/25392809.gif" alt="chop chop" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not Keiko Furukura! After 18 years, she's so well attuned to the sounds of the convenience store, that she can react even to the slightest change in her environment. A soft jiggle of small change, generally means a quick transaction for a pack of cigarettes. A nearby competitor going out of business, means a sudden increase in customers. Time to stock up on the best selling merchandise.<br><br>Our heroine has always struggled to fit in, never quite attaining the state of "normalcy" dictated by society. Life as a convenience store employee however, is just perfect for her. With a clear set of rules to follow, our heroine has a fool-proof template applicable in any situation. If only the rest of the world would let her be...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523994020ra/25392807.gif" alt="annoyed flayling" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aw man, did I get <em>mad</em> at society during the course of this story. I was in a constant state of rage towards Keiko's 'entourage'. I mean, she is brilliant at her job, just plain perfectly in tune with the store's every need, and yet her coworkers are stuck on the details of her personal life. <strong>*screams*</strong><br><br>I got truly involved in the whole action, and started perceiving every slight, as if people had been criticizing <em>me</em>. I even felt totally in tune with Keiko's brand of weirdness, earnestly trying to find extenuating circumstances for each and every oddity.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1523994020i/25392808._SX540_.jpg" alt="Musette and her reading choices" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><em>Musette preparing to dive into parallel reading</em><br><br>I had initially requested the German ARC from NetGalley, but after two weeks of radio silence I figured I wouldn't be getting it. So when I saw the Romanian translation in a bookstore, I all but jumped at the opportunity to buy it... only to get my NetGalley request approved the very same day. <br>Impatience, thy name is indeed: <em>Smartarse</em>.<br><br>Long story short: I felt pressured to read both versions. So I did. In parallel. I can't say it was a particularly good idea, but doable with such a short book.<br><br><strong>Score: 4.9/5 stars</strong><br><br>I prefer the German version to the Romanian one. The rigid atmosphere of the Japanese society came to life much better here, along with Keiko's overly detached view of the world. Alternately, my German's not good enough to grasp all the language subtleties, so any blanks in comprehension were filled in with wishful thinking. <br><br>Either way, both versions felt well translated.<br><br>---------------<br><em>German ARC provided by <a href="http://netgalley.de" rel="nofollow noopener">NetGalleyDE</a> and <a href="http://www.aufbau-verlag.de/" rel="nofollow noopener">Aufbau Verlag</a>, in exchange for an honest and fair review.</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="2691050715494347408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1455831683247847188"> <b>“More than a person, I’m a convenience store worker. Even if that means I’m abnormal and can’t make a living and drop down dead, I can’t escape that fact. My very cells exist for the convenience store.”</b><br/><br/>Sayaka Murata’s Convenience Store Woman immediately immerses the reader into the world of the Japanese convenience store, what it stocks, the quirks of its patrons and its idiosyncratic rhythm. We also quickly learn that for our protagonist, Keiko Furukura, this is the only world that makes sense</span>
  <span id="freeText1455831683247847188" style="display:none"> <b>“More than a person, I’m a convenience store worker. Even if that means I’m abnormal and can’t make a living and drop down dead, I can’t escape that fact. My very cells exist for the convenience store.”</b><br /><br />Sayaka Murata’s Convenience Store Woman immediately immerses the reader into the world of the Japanese convenience store, what it stocks, the quirks of its patrons and its idiosyncratic rhythm. We also quickly learn that for our protagonist, Keiko Furukura, this is the only world that makes sense. Keiko understands that she’s not normal, but can’t seem to do anything about it. As her part-time job (which began when she was in college) extends to define her life as a 36-year old with no prospects, others alternately try to fix and ostracize her. This was a short but engaging read! <br /></span>

<div id="review_2343243746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2343243746" />
    <a title="Vanessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25545124-vanessa"><img alt="Vanessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505021049p2/25545124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2343243746?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa" href="/user/show/25545124-vanessa">Vanessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780802128256" href="/book/show/36739755-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2343243746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4102939252304849419">Convenience store woman is a simple little story about Keiko Furukura a totally quirky hopelessly inept character but in a totally charming and sweet way. She’s a character that defies societies norms by bucking the traditional role designated for women that require them to have a “proper” or “normal” job, a husband and children by a certain age. I felt a deep sadness for Keiko always being subjected to judgement and how she was always making excuses for her life choices. I felt a real tug on my</span>
  <span id="freeText4102939252304849419" style="display:none">Convenience store woman is a simple little story about Keiko Furukura a totally quirky hopelessly inept character but in a totally charming and sweet way. She’s a character that defies societies norms by bucking the traditional role designated for women that require them to have a “proper” or “normal” job, a husband and children by a certain age. I felt a deep sadness for Keiko always being subjected to judgement and how she was always making excuses for her life choices. I felt a real tug on my heartstrings. I ended up totally in love with this character. So many times I wanted to wrap Keiko up in cotton wool and protect her from those relentless judgemental eyes. Reading this made me angry, really angry! The fact this was set in Japan also made me love this book just that little bit more as I adore the Japanese culture, and the few books I’ve read from there have always been a delight. What first appears to be a simple story of a simple woman living her simple life really becomes an examination of society’s pressures and the damage it can cause people who don’t fit in to that mould. This book may be small in size but it has a big heart.<br /><br />Thanks to Netgalley and Grove Atlantic for my review copy. Pub date 22 June 2018.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4102939252304849419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3331321912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3331321912" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3331321912?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/51031906-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3331321912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15187883669310581207"><blockquote>“The normal world has no room for exceptions and always quietly eliminates foreign objects. Anyone who is lacking is disposed of.”</blockquote><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38357895.Convenience_Store_Woman' title='Convenience Store Woman by Sayaka Murata' rel='nofollow noopener'> Convenience Store Woman</a> tells the store of Keiko Furukura, a 36 year-old woman who has worked in a convenience store for half of her life. While her family and friends go to university, get married, have children and do what is viewed by society as 'normal,' Keiko follows her own routine. She works passionately for a convenience store, following the employee manual, </span>
  <span id="freeText15187883669310581207" style="display:none"><blockquote>“The normal world has no room for exceptions and always quietly eliminates foreign objects. Anyone who is lacking is disposed of.”</blockquote><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38357895.Convenience_Store_Woman" title="Convenience Store Woman by Sayaka Murata" rel="nofollow noopener"> Convenience Store Woman</a> tells the store of Keiko Furukura, a 36 year-old woman who has worked in a convenience store for half of her life. While her family and friends go to university, get married, have children and do what is viewed by society as 'normal,' Keiko follows her own routine. She works passionately for a convenience store, following the employee manual, greeting customers with a smile, ensuring all products are neatly arranged and easily accessible, and overall doing her work to the best of her abilities. But that just isn't enough for society who views her as odd and somehow 'behind' for still working there after eighteen years. <br /><br />Keiko is a very endearing, likeable narrator. To the outside world she may be odd, but to the reader—or at least this reader—she was perfectly understandable. She may be wired different, but Keiko proves that different doesn't mean bad. It simply means dancing to your own rhythm. Along the way, she encounters blips in the system that force her to confront her reality and determine what is truly right for her life, regardless of what others might believe. Sometimes staying true to yourself means going against the majority, and it was refreshing to read about a character who may not project confidence to the world but finds confidence in themself. <br /><br />The translation, by Ginny Tapley Takemori, is well done. I felt alive while reading this in the way that Keiko feels alive in her workplace. I never noticed anything odd in translation to pull me out of the story, which I'd deem a success.<br /><br />While I can see why some people may be turned off by the oddities of this story and the sometimes brusque or straightforward nature of the characters, I found them charming and intriguing. Plus it's a very short novel, so I'd recommend you give it a shot if it sounds interesting to you. Maybe you'll find something inspiring in Keiko like I did! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15187883669310581207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2415258530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2415258530" />
    <a title="Jane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39215947-jane"><img alt="Jane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526919066p2/39215947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2415258530?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane" href="/user/show/39215947-jane">Jane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780802128256" href="/book/show/36739755-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39215947-jane?shelf=znetgalley-challenge-2018">znetgalley-challenge-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39215947-jane?shelf=z2018">z2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39215947-jane?shelf=non-kindle-kindle">non-kindle-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39215947-jane?shelf=1netgalley">1netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2415258530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16956527357958952494">4.5 pleasantly surprised stars for this intriguing little book! <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36605525.Convenience_Store_Woman' title='Convenience Store Woman by Sayaka Murata' rel='nofollow noopener'>Convenience Store Woman</a> is not action-packed nor steeped in drama, but it is a compelling read nonetheless. <br/><br/>The story follows Keiko Furukura, a 36-year-old, part-time convenience store employee. The people in her life have always thought she is a little odd, and yet they are perplexed by her seeming inability to move beyond what is seen as a temporary life stage. Keiko, on the other hand, doesn't know why anyone should care that she</span>
  <span id="freeText16956527357958952494" style="display:none">4.5 pleasantly surprised stars for this intriguing little book! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36605525.Convenience_Store_Woman" title="Convenience Store Woman by Sayaka Murata" rel="nofollow noopener">Convenience Store Woman</a> is not action-packed nor steeped in drama, but it is a compelling read nonetheless. <br /><br />The story follows Keiko Furukura, a 36-year-old, part-time convenience store employee. The people in her life have always thought she is a little odd, and yet they are perplexed by her seeming inability to move beyond what is seen as a temporary life stage. Keiko, on the other hand, doesn't know why anyone should care that she has found contentment in the predictability of her work, and the comfort brought by the rules in the employee manual.<br /><br />I'm not exactly sure how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8816506.Sayaka_Murata" title="Sayaka Murata" rel="nofollow noopener">Sayaka Murata</a> managed to write such a captivating account of what is basically the daily routine of a worker in a convenience store, but I could not put this book down! Keiko was a fascinating character, and by the time this (much too short!) story was done, I found myself rooting for her to live her life her own damn way, weirdness and all.<br /><br />I'll definitely be watching for more from this author -- her talent is incredible.<br /><br />Badass Female Character score: 5/5 -- Keiko's living life her own way and shows strength even when others wish she were more "normal".<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley and Grove Atlantic for providing me with an e-ARC of this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16956527357958952494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338391096?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36605525-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338391096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5764383479293571559"><b>FIVE STARS</b><br/>What a strange and quirky little book this is! This is a kind of Japanese version of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31434883.Eleanor_Oliphant_Is_Completely_Fine' title='Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine by Gail Honeyman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine</a>. I love to read contemporary books set in different cultures and this is one, set in Tokyo, is ideal! Can I just say, American convenience stores have a long way to go to live up to Japanese stores in terms of cleanliness, well-trained and friendly staff, etc etc!!<br/><br/>Keiko Furukura is hopelessly out-of-step with societal expectations of women. In a culture that values c</span>
  <span id="freeText5764383479293571559" style="display:none"><b>FIVE STARS</b><br />What a strange and quirky little book this is! This is a kind of Japanese version of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31434883.Eleanor_Oliphant_Is_Completely_Fine" title="Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine by Gail Honeyman" rel="nofollow noopener">Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine</a>. I love to read contemporary books set in different cultures and this is one, set in Tokyo, is ideal! Can I just say, American convenience stores have a long way to go to live up to Japanese stores in terms of cleanliness, well-trained and friendly staff, etc etc!!<br /><br />Keiko Furukura is hopelessly out-of-step with societal expectations of women. In a culture that values conformist behavior, she struggles until she finds her first job working in the convenience store. After many years of working part time at the store and living alone, she experiments with fitting in to please her family. It doesn't exactly work out, but, she eventually figures out her own way to happiness. <br /><br />I don't want to say more than that since the book is so short! It is really a charming, sweet story of Keiko's pursuit for acceptance. Sayaka Murata is a wonderful writer and wrote this story while she herself was working in a convenience store (and still does!). While I wish the book was longer, it is actually perfect the way it is. <br /><br /><i>Scheduled for US publication in June 2018. Many thanks to NetGalley for allowing me to read and review this darling book!</i></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40778245-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2454950879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5635006049642888560"><b>If you love witty conversation, wry humor and quirky characters then Convenience Store Woman is the book for you! </b><br/><br/>Originally written in Japanese, <b>Convenience Store Woman</b> on the surface is a story about Keiko Furukura, a woman whose own parents labeled "a strange child." Slow to develop, Keiko's parents were worried about her ability to "fit in" and be a "normal" adult. They wish for Keiko to have a "real job" and a boyfriend. However, Keiko loves her job at the convenience store and her only wor</span>
  <span id="freeText5635006049642888560" style="display:none"><b>If you love witty conversation, wry humor and quirky characters then Convenience Store Woman is the book for you! </b><br /><br />Originally written in Japanese, <b>Convenience Store Woman</b> on the surface is a story about Keiko Furukura, a woman whose own parents labeled "a strange child." Slow to develop, Keiko's parents were worried about her ability to "fit in" and be a "normal" adult. They wish for Keiko to have a "real job" and a boyfriend. However, Keiko loves her job at the convenience store and her only worry is the pressure to live up to her parents' expectations.<br /><br />As the characters come and go through the store, we soon realize that perhaps Keiko is the one who comes closest to "normal."<br /><br /><b>Convenience Store Woman</b> is an endearing story, a character study of a myriad of personalities and a tale of acceptance that will warm your heart and leave you wanting more. It also is a wonderful, subtle opportunity to catch a glimpse of the Japanese culture.<br /><br />This is a beautiful, very short piece of fiction by Sayaka Murata, who still works part time at a convenience store.<br /><br />My thanks to #Netgalley, the author, Granta Publications and Portobello Books for the opportunity to read this intriguing book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6127525866348424782">I have seen this described as the Japanese Eleanor Oliphant, because Keiko, the central character, doesn't know how to act in "normal" situations, and hasn't been able to, even as a child. A quick read with an interesting character.<br/><br/><i>I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. It comes out 12 June, 2018.</i></span>

<div id="review_2500553131" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2500553131" />
    <a title="PorshaJo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5464046-porshajo"><img alt="PorshaJo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451425289p2/5464046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2500553131?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PorshaJo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PorshaJo" href="/user/show/5464046-porshajo">PorshaJo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780802128256" href="/book/show/36739755-convenience-store-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=challengereads-2018">challengereads-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=challengereads">challengereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=culture-japanese">culture-japanese</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2500553131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14872169999682136253">Rating 3.5<br/><br/>Odd, fascinating, funny, sad....trying to sum this one is difficult. A short story that I listened to via audio, which took about 3 hours in total. I'm not sure how I heard about this one but ended up grabbing it for my Japanese reading quest I have this year.<br/><br/>Keiko works in a Japanese convenience store. She's a bit odd. She's smart, but it sometimes appears she has issues functioning in society. But she thrives while working at the convenience store. She gets a job there and stays for </span>
  <span id="freeText14872169999682136253" style="display:none">Rating 3.5<br /><br />Odd, fascinating, funny, sad....trying to sum this one is difficult. A short story that I listened to via audio, which took about 3 hours in total. I'm not sure how I heard about this one but ended up grabbing it for my Japanese reading quest I have this year.<br /><br />Keiko works in a Japanese convenience store. She's a bit odd. She's smart, but it sometimes appears she has issues functioning in society. But she thrives while working at the convenience store. She gets a job there and stays for 18 years. But culture dictates she should be married, having kids, doing more....conforming to the standards. But she doesn't feel the need to. She's happy. But all of a sudden, she is convinced by someone like her (a bit odd, issues functioning) to help him "conform" and eventually leave the convenience store. Where she ultimately looses her purpose. It's interesting to have this look at the Japanese culture to conform (but really, isn't it everywhere) to society and their expectations. I felt sad for Keiko, seeing what she went through, and wanting people just to let her be, she was happy. And quite the interesting look at Japanese convenience stores, and if memory is correct, are VERY different from those in the US.<br /><br />The audio narration was wonderful. I really enjoyed listening to this one. I just wanted more from the story, I wanted to know more are Keiko. Overall, glad I picked this one up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14872169999682136253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pbrucWS7OScIVf1FiDdayfyxKjHiaAIdkSEtcKdk2wB/cWi/tUupqV9sTCDlxH4PFoNmFRrVIzpn5v2yaBkf3g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2SKg4NK1RoGyL0k4wjVK+7gFMjWu2JSl3ecBs2F0e7oD6SYuA0XWD+UW+F2vxm49Ujd+EVZltYIrINFxrgm/ZA==')})
  }

프로그램에<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5772419759705140346\" style=\"display:none\">“사람들이 나보고 맘충이래.” 한국에서 여자로 살아가는 일 그 공포, 피로, 당황, 놀람, 혼란, 좌절의 연속에 대한 인생 현장 보고서 조남주 장편소설 『82년생 김지영』이 민음사 ‘오늘의 젊은 작가’ 시리즈로 출간되었다. 조남주 작가는 2011년, 지적 장애가 있는 한 소년의 재능이 발견되면서 벌어지는 사건을 통해 삶의 부조리를 현실적이면서도 따뜻하게 그려낸 작품 『귀를 귀울이면』으로 ‘문학동네소설상’을 받으며 데뷔했다. 시사 교양 프로그램에서 10년 동안 일한 방송 작가답게 서민들의 일상에서 발생하는 비극을 사실적이고 공감대 높은 스토리로 표현하는 데 특출 난 재능을 보이는 작가는 신작 『82년생 김지영』에서 30대를 살고 있는 한국 여성들의 보편적인 일상을 완벽하게 재현한다. 주인공 ‘김지영 씨’의 기억을 바탕으로 한 고백을 한 축으로, 고백을 뒷받침하는 각종 통계 자료와 기사들을 또 다른 축으로 삼는 이 소설은 1982년생 김지영 씨로 대변되는 ‘그녀’들의 인생 마디마디에 존재하는 성차별적 요소를 핍진하게 묘사한다. 이를 통해 작가는 제도적 성차별이 줄어든 시대의 보이지 않는 차별들이 어떻게 여성들의 삶을 제약하고 억압하는지 보여 준다. 여권이 신장된 시대, 그러나 여전히 ‘여성’이라는 조건이 굴레로 존재하는 사회에서 살아가는 한 여자의 인생을 다룬 『82년생 김지영』은 조용한 고백과 뜨거운 고발로 완성된 새로운 페미니즘 소설이자 수많은 사람들의 경험과 자료로 이루어진 ‘목소리 소설’이다. 맘충이, 여혐, 메갈리아 등 연일 새롭게 등장하는 페미니즘 화두를 관심 있게 지켜보는 독자라면 누구나 흥미롭게 읽을 수 있고 저마다 의미를 발견할 수 있을 것이다<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5772419759705140346\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8816506.Sayaka_Murata">About Sayaka Murata</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8816506.Sayaka_Murata"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1522684114p3/8816506.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8816506.Sayaka_Murata">Sayaka Murata
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,370
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10178240735875079402">Sayaka Murata (in Japanese, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7457319.______' title='村田 沙耶香' rel='nofollow noopener'>村田 沙耶香</a>) is one of the most exciting up-and-coming writers in Japan today. She herself still works part time in a convenience store, which gave her the inspiration to write <i>Convenience Store Woman</i> (<i>Conbini Ningen</i>). She debuted in 2003 with <i>Junyu</i> (<i>Breastfeeding</i>), which won the Gunzo Prize for new writers. In 2009 she won the Noma Prize for New Writers with <i>Gin iro no uta</i> </span>
  <span id="freeText10178240735875079402" style="display:none">Sayaka Murata (in Japanese, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7457319.______" title="村田 沙耶香" rel="nofollow noopener">村田 沙耶香</a>) is one of the most exciting up-and-coming writers in Japan today. She herself still works part time in a convenience store, which gave her the inspiration to write <i>Convenience Store Woman</i> (<i>Conbini Ningen</i>). She debuted in 2003 with <i>Junyu</i> (<i>Breastfeeding</i>), which won the Gunzo Prize for new writers. In 2009 she won the Noma Prize for New Writers with <i>Gin iro no uta</i> (<i>Silver Song</i>), and in 2013 the Mishima Yukio Prize for <i>Shiro-oro no machi no, sono hone no taion no</i> (<i>Of Bones, of Body Heat, of Whitening City</i>). <i>Convenience Store Woman</i> won the 2016 Akutagawa Award. Murata has two short stories published in English (both translated by Ginny Tapley Takemori): "Lover on the Breeze" (<i>Ruptured Fiction(s) of the Earthquake</i>, Waseda Bungaku, 2011) and "A Clean Marriage" (<i>Granta 127: Japan</i>, 2014).</span>
  <a data-text-id="10178240735875079402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
